msg:We stayed at the Shangri-la after a week of being in Tibet. It was a nice change from the more Chinese style hotels we had stayed in and was ideal for the night before our flight out. The rooms are great and we booked one with a bath. The shower was very powerful and hot. The breakfast buffet was, by Chinese standards, decent for western options and the evening buffer was good for approx 200rmb/person if you're in need of more western options.

The big plus for me was the gym. Decent by most hotel standards and had a good mix of resistance machines, cardio and free weights (mainly dumbbells of up to 20kg plus a pair of 27.5kg). The only thing missing from the gym really is a squat rack but otherwise very good. Would stay again.

So I have to choose a hotel that is close to the scenic area, has an oxygen generator room, good sound insulation, and a medical room. Finally, I chose Shangri-La Hotel. It was really right. Before I checked in, Xiao Deng, the front desk of Shangri-La, called to ask me about my room requirements, told me some precautions for coming to Lhasa, and gave me breakfast for check-in. After checking in, I found that the room was relatively large, clean and odorless. The sound insulation effect was good, and I slept very well during my stay. I was almost embarrassed to ask Xiao Deng for two cans of oxygen every day. But taking oxygen out can indeed reduce altitude sickness. There is also a special oxygen bar on the first floor, which can relieve altitude sickness. There is an oxygen generator in the room, and later I asked for another one. Both of us can relieve altitude sickness, which is very good. The breakfast is also very rich, and the butter tea is delicious. Maybe everyone's experience of staying is different. It takes 50 minutes to take a taxi to the airport. There is an open-air terrace where you can have afternoon tea in the hotel, and you can overlook the Potala Palace in the distance, which is quite nice. The room layout is very ******* style, with an oxygen concentrator. There is an infirmary on the first floor of the hotel. If you feel uncomfortable, you can go there at any time. You can also rent oxygen tanks. Outside pharmacies and medical equipment stores do not rent oxygen tanks. They sell them directly. You can rent them 24 hours a day here. I am I only found out after I went to see a doctor when I wasn't feeling well. The hotel's breakfast is very rich, including ******* tsampa, butter tea, sweet tea, highland barley cakes, and handmade yogurt. You can try it. The fruits also change every day. Remember to eat more fruits with high sugar content in Tibet. I ate the special Medog stone pot yak beef at the hotel's Chinese restaurant Shang Palace. Two people can order half portion. The soup is very fragrant and the beef is delicious. Finally, let me talk about the hotel service staff. They are very enthusiastic. They will say hello when they see you and answer all your questions. Especially before you check into the hotel, a dedicated housekeeper will contact you and provide service and answers to the guests throughout the entire process. This is really good and makes people feel safe and secure. Our housekeeper is named Danya, which is great. We are in Lhasa. He was able to help us solve all our problems within three days, so thumbs up. I am very satisfied with my choice of Shangri-La when I came to Lhasa this time.

msg:I have stayed at St. Regis, Songtsan and Shangri-La. I hope this review can provide some reference for those who are struggling between the three like me.

Let me start with the conclusion: For those who need to visit scenic spots, Shangri-La is the first choice; for those who like to stay in the hotel and want to experience ******* culture, you can consider Songtsan; St. Regis will destroy your previous good impression of St. Regis

Location:
Shangri-La is close to the Tibet Museum, Norbulingka, and Potala Palace, which can be reached on foot. 5 stars
St. Regis is close to Barkhor Street, which can be reached on foot. 5 stars
Songtsan is far away. Except for watching the performance of Princess Wencheng, it is far away from everything. 3 stars

Service:
All service staff of Songtsan are ******* friends, which is unique, but the service details and processes are not very smooth. It is still a little weaker than international chains, but it wins in sincerity. 4 stars+

The service of St. Regis is acceptable, 5 stars

Shangri-La is very good. Generally, the service level in Tibet is worse than that in the mainland, but Shangri-La is not, especially the manager Nan Nan, who is very professional, meticulous and gentle. He almost responds to every request. Thank you very much 5 stars +

A small detail, my friend and I were on the same flight, and the subsequent flight was cancelled, so we needed to refund the first day's room fee. My friend stayed at St. Regis, and he had to get a delay certificate at the airport, but Shangri-La just sent a screenshot of the text message and immediately helped with the formalities. In terms of small details, Xiangxiang is obviously more humane

Hotel hardware and environment:

Songzan is the most distinctive, with pure *******-style small buildings like resort hotels, which are very beautiful and distinctive; I booked the Potala Palace Deluxe Suite, and the room has a small balcony, which is very impressive, but the so-called Potala Palace view is actually very small because it is far away, and a new house has been built in front of the hotel, which may be other hotels, and the view is blocked, not as good as the official picture. 5 stars

St. Regis is the most helpless to complain about. The Japanese designer obviously has a little misunderstanding of ******* architecture. The whole architectural style is very gloomy. Refer to the opening ceremony in Tokyo, and the room is also spooky. In addition, the hotel's daily maintenance is not very good. The wood in the elevator is peeling, the room curtains are very cheap, and the blinds are tied with black insulating tape when the rope is broken.

I can only say that the official photos of St. Regis are more 4 stars

Shangri-La is a modified ******* building, which is a combination of the conventional Shangri-La style and the ******* style, but I think it is just right, retaining the national characteristics while retaining modern comfort. It is worth mentioning that the hotel is very well maintained, that is, you can't feel that this is a hotel in Tibet (refer to St. Regis, no comparison, no harm) 5 stars

Landscape:
Shangri-La Libu Palace Recently, I stayed in the landscape king bed and landscape executive. The window is the Bu Palace. The feeling of sitting by the window and reading a book is not too happy 5 stars +

Most of the rooms and suites of St. Regis have no view. I originally booked the executive room, and I felt that the room had no view (street) and it was more gloomy when I entered. I wanted to pay more to change to a suite, but the staff persuaded me that the suite was darker, and there was no view unless it was a top suite. 3 stars

Songtsan View Suite can see the Potala Palace but it is far away and blocked 4 stars +

Food:
If there is any aspect of Shangri-La that can be better, it should be the food!

I stayed for 7 days this time, and the breakfast did not change. The products were so-so, and the fried dough sticks and fried cakes were dry and hard, and they did not feel very fresh. Of course, I can understand that there are fewer tourists in the off-season recently, but it was not very good when I came during the peak season last year. Hahaha

The Chinese restaurant is average

4 stars

Songtsan‚Äôs breakfast is the most impressive. There are not many varieties, but they change every day, and the products are very good. The restaurant service is very good and warm

The ******* restaurant has nothing to say about the products. Lunch and dinner are basically solved here.

5 stars

I stayed at the St. Regis in August last year. The breakfast is better than Shangri-La, and I don‚Äôt have a special impression

5 stars
